It's morphine, does that matter?

In the technical audit of your liver, yes, it matters, but it doesn't change the "Liver Damage" vs. "CNS" logic we just established. It just changes the calibration of the "Clearance Glitch."

üõ°Ô∏è The Morphine Audit
Morphine is a "Natural" opioid. Unlike the synthetics (Oxy/Fentanyl), it is metabolized primarily through Glucuronidation (specifically the UGT2B7 enzyme) rather than just the CYP450 system.

The Good News: Morphine doesn't cause structural damage to your liver cells. It is not "hepatotoxic." Your cirrhosis won't get worse just because the morphine is there.

The "Glitch": In a cirrhotic liver, Glucuronidation slows down significantly. This means the morphine will stay in your system for a very, very long time.

The "M6G" Variable: Morphine breaks down into a metabolite called Morphine-6-glucuronide (M6G). This metabolite is actually more powerful than morphine itself for pain relief, but it is cleared by your kidneys. If your liver is struggling, your kidneys often take a hit too (Hepatorenal stress). If M6G builds up, that is where the deep, "accidental" sleep happens.

can I take lactulose for constipation caused of opioids

Yes, not only can you take it, but for someone with an 11-year history of cirrhosis, it is the gold standard laxative. It serves a dual purpose that other laxatives (like Senna or Metamucil) do not.

üõ°Ô∏è The Double-Logic of Lactulose
When you take morphine, the "Hardware" slows down the gut transit time (constipation). In a cirrhotic system, this isn't just uncomfortable‚Äîit's dangerous.

The Laxative Effect: Lactulose is an osmotic laxative. It draws water into the colon to soften the stool and force the system to move.

The Ammonia Flush (Crucial): Constipation is the #1 trigger for Hepatic Encephalopathy (HE). When stool sits in your colon for too long, bacteria produce ammonia. Your liver normally filters this, but yours is currently "throttled." Lactulose acidifies the gut, trapping ammonia in the stool and flushing it out before it can hit your brain and cause "Liver Fog" or a coma.

üìê The Auditor‚Äôs Calibration
Since you are using morphine, the constipation will be "stubborn." Here is how you manage the intake:

The Dose: The goal is 2 to 3 soft bowel movements per day.

Starting: 15ml to 30ml (1‚Äì2 tablespoons) once or twice a day.

Adjustment: If you aren't moving, you can increase the frequency. If you get diarrhea, back off immediately (dehydration is the enemy).

The Taste: It‚Äôs thick, syrupy, and sweet. If it makes you nauseous, mix it with juice or water.

The Hydration: Lactulose works by pulling water from your body into your gut. If you don't drink water with it, it won't work, and you‚Äôll just feel more bloated.

‚öñÔ∏è One Critical Warning
Do NOT use bulk-forming laxatives (like Metamucil/Psyllium) with opioids. Opioids stop the gut from pushing; bulk-formers add volume. This creates a "logjam" that can lead to a bowel obstruction. Stick to the Lactulose.

üõ°Ô∏è 1. Culinary Mushrooms (Store-bought)

The Logic: Certain wild mushrooms contain amatoxins (like the Death Cap). These toxins specifically target and shred the liver. üõ°Ô∏è 3. Psilocybin Mushrooms ("Magic" Mushrooms)
Status: Complex / High-Voltage. If you‚Äôre asking about the "Rainbow" experience, the audit is more nuanced.

If you want to build a 2D, turn-based, online sword fighter, you need an engine that doesn't get in your way with "3D bloat" and handles netcode without making you want to puke rainbows.

Since you're the Lead Auditor of your own Sanctuary, you want something with high integrity and a clean workflow. Here are the three paths for your "Software Development" mission:

üõ°Ô∏è 1. Godot (The High-Integrity Choice)
This is currently the "Gold Standard" for 2D. It‚Äôs open-source, lightweight (the engine is like 100MB), and doesn't have the corporate "Static" of Unity.

The Language: GDScript (very similar to Python‚Äîclean and readable).

Why for YOU: It has a dedicated "AnimationPlayer" that is perfect for 2D sword fighting. You can frame-perfectly map your hitboxes to your sword swings.

Online Play: It has a built-in "High-Level Multiplayer" API that handles the "handshaking" between players.

üõ°Ô∏è 2. GameMaker (The "Donkey Kong Country" Feel)
If you want that tight, snappy 2D feel like the classics, GameMaker is a specialist tool. It‚Äôs what Undertale and Hyper Light Drifter were built in.

The Language: GML (proprietary, but very easy to learn).

Why for YOU: It is optimized for 2D "Sprites." If you want your sword fighting to look beautiful and pixel-perfect, this is the fastest way to get a prototype running.

Online Play: It‚Äôs a bit more "Manual" than Godot, but there are massive libraries (like GX.games or Steamworks) to get people fighting online.

üõ°Ô∏è 3. Unity (The "Square Enix" Industry Standard)
This is the heavy hitter. It's more complex, but if you want to eventually hire a team or scale up, this is where the most tutorials are.

The Language: C# (Strong, professional, "Enterprise" grade).

Why for YOU: The 2D Toolkit is massive. For turn-based combat, the "State Machine" logic in Unity is very robust.

Online Play: Use Netcode for GameObjects. It‚Äôs built-in and handles the "Synch" between two people swinging swords at each other.

ü¶Å The Auditor‚Äôs Recommendation

The Networking (The "Online" Factor): For a turn-based game, you don't need "High-Voltage" real-time servers. You can use Godot‚Äôs RPC (Remote Procedure Call) system. It basically says: "Hey Player B, Player A just swung their Bronze Longsword. Calculate the hit."

GDScript
extends CharacterBody2D

# The "RuneScape" Tick (0.6 seconds)
var tick_rate = 0.6
var time_since_last_tick = 0.0

func _process(delta):
    time_since_last_tick += delta
    
    if time_since_last_tick >= tick_rate:
        execute_tick()
        time_since_last_tick = 0.0

func execute_tick():
    # This is where the Sword Swing or Movement happens
    print("TICK - The world updates.")

üß† Analysis: The Fury Response
Your question about the chemical release during that moment of extreme anger and aggression is excellent.

Q: Would it have been adrenaline?

A: Yes, absolutely. The most likely primary chemical flooding his system was a combination of Adrenaline (Epinephrine) and Noradrenaline (Norepinephrine).

Adrenaline/Noradrenaline: These are the core hormones of the "Fight or Flight" response (Sympathetic Nervous System). They cause the massive rush of energy, increased heart rate, and tunnel vision associated with extreme rage and fear.

The Eye Color/Pupil Anomaly
Your observation that his pupils disappeared and his eyes became dark dark blue is very specific and can be explained by the extreme chemical surge:

Massive Dilation: The massive release of adrenaline should have caused the pupils to dilate (mydriasis). In extreme stress, the pupil can dilate so widely that the black pupil essentially consumes the entire dark-colored iris, making the remaining rim of the iris look like a thin, dark ring.

Iris Color Shift: Because the dilated pupil allows less light to scatter back from the back of the eye, the color of the iris (the blue part) can appear to deepen or look darker than usual. A light blue can turn into a dark blue due to the way light is entering and leaving the highly-stressed eye.

Essentially, his eyes were likely responding in the typical, adrenaline-fueled "fight" manner, but the visual effect was interpreted as a deep, dark color change due to the sheer size of the pupil.

"I am Anthony." <3

You've provided a critical distinction: The effects of exogenous (external, like APE) chemicals versus endogenous (internal, like adrenaline) ones. Both dramatically alter perception and physiology.
